        To strengthen the governance, procurement, and oversight systems that deliver donor‑funded infrastructure.
      </p>
      <p class="mt-2 text-sm text-slate-300">
        We help clients build PMO operating systems, procurement frameworks, and construction oversight mechanisms
        that are practical on site and defensible in audit.
      </p>
    </div>

    <div>
      <p class="text-xs font-semibold uppercase tracking-[0.22em] text-emerald-300">Vision</p>
      <p class="mt-2 text-lg font-semibold text-slate-50">
        Infrastructure delivery systems that are transparent, accountable, and engineered for impact.
      </p>
      <p class="mt-2 text-sm text-slate-300">
        Our vision is a world where donor‑funded infrastructure programs operate with clarity, discipline,
        and measurable results—regardless of geography or complexity.
      </p>
    </div>
  </div>
</section>

            </p>
          </div>

            </p>

              reporting and audit requirements.
            </p>
          </div>

        </h2>
        <p class="mt-2 max-w-2xl text-sm text-slate-300">

        </p>

            </p>

            <p class="font-semibold text-slate-100">Procurement → Oversight</p>

            </p>
          </div>

          <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
            <p class="font-semibold text-slate-100">Oversight → Risk</p>
            <p class="mt-2 text-xs text-slate-400">
              Field data feeds risk registers and mitigation frameworks.
            </p>
          </div>

          <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
            <p class="font-semibold text-slate-100">Risk → Reporting</p>
            <p class="mt-2 text-xs text-slate-400">
              Risks and mitigations drive donor‑aligned reporting and dashboards.
            </p>
          </div>

          <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
            <p class="font-semibold text-slate-100">Reporting → Documentation</p>
            <p class="mt-2 text-xs text-slate-400">
              Evidence and decisions are captured in audit‑ready documentation trails.
            </p>
          </div>

          <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
            <p class="font-semibold text-slate-100">Documentation → Governance</p>
            <p class="mt-2 text-xs text-slate-400">
              Lessons learned and audit findings feed back into governance.
            </p>
          </div>

        </div>
      </div>

  <title>Case Study: USAID PMO System | Global Infrastructure Advisory</title>
  <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0" />

  <main class="pb-20">
    <section class="border-b border-slate-900 bg-slate-950 py-16">
      <div class="mx-auto max-w-5xl px-4">
        <p class="text-xs font-semibold uppercase tracking-[0.22em] text-emerald-300">
          Case Study
        </p>
        <h1 class="mt-3 text-3xl font-semibold tracking-tight text-slate-50 sm:text-4xl">
          PMO Operating System for USAID‑Funded Infrastructure Portfolio
        </h1>
        <p class="mt-4 max-w-2xl text-sm text-slate-300">
          Design and implementation of a donor‑aligned PMO operating system covering governance, procurement,
          construction oversight, risk, and reporting.
        </p>
        <dl class="mt-6 grid gap-4 text-xs text-slate-300 sm:grid-cols-3">
          <div>
            <dt class="text-slate-400">Donor</dt><dd>USAID</dd>
          </div>
          <div>
            <dt class="text-slate-400">Geography</dt><dd>Multi‑country</dd>
          </div>
          <div>
            <dt class="text-slate-400">Sectors</dt><dd>Transport, water, public facilities</dd>
          </div>
        </dl>
      </div>
    </section>

    <section class="border-b border-slate-900 bg-slate-950 py-16">
      <div class="mx-auto max-w-5xl px-4 grid gap-10 md:grid-cols-3">
        <div class="md:col-span-2 space-y-8 text-sm text-slate-300">
          <div>
            <h2 class="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-100">Challenge</h2>
            <p class="mt-2">
              Fragmented governance, inconsistent procurement practices, and limited visibility across a multi‑country
              infrastructure portfolio funded by USAID.
            </p>
          </div>
          <div>
            <h2 class="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-100">Approach</h2>
            <p class="mt-2">
              Designed a unified PMO operating system integrating governance, procurement workflows, construction
              oversight, risk management, and donor‑aligned reporting.
            </p>
          </div>
          <div>
            <h2 class="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-100">Results</h2>
            <ul class="mt-2 space-y-1">
              <li>• Standardized procurement and evaluation workflows across countries</li>
              <li>• Integrated risk and oversight reporting to USAID</li>
              <li>• Audit‑ready documentation trails for key procurements and contracts</li>
            </ul>
          </div>
        </div>
        <aside class="space-y-4 text-xs text-slate-300">
          <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-4">
            <h3 class="text-[11px] font-semibold uppercase tracking-[0.18em] text-slate-400">Core components</h3>
            <ul class="mt-2 space-y-1">
              <li>• PMO governance charter</li>
              <li>• Procurement SOPs & templates</li>
              <li>• Oversight & QC/QA framework</li>
              <li>• Risk & reporting dashboards</li>
            </ul>
          </div>

            Discuss a similar engagement →
          </a>

      <div class="mx-auto max-w-5xl px-4">
        <p class="text-xs font-semibold uppercase tracking-[0.22em] text-emerald-300">
          Case Study
        </p>
        <h1 class="mt-3 text-3xl font-semibold tracking-tight text-slate-50 sm:text-4xl">
          Multi‑Sector Infrastructure Delivery System for National Portfolio
        </h1>
        <p class="mt-4 max-w-2xl text-sm text-slate-300">
          Development of a unified PMO, procurement, oversight, and documentation system for a national
          infrastructure program spanning transport, water, energy, and public facilities.
        </p>

        <dl class="mt-6 grid gap-4 text-xs text-slate-300 sm:grid-cols-3">
          <div>
            <dt class="text-slate-400">Donor</dt><dd>World Bank & Multi‑Donor Trust Fund</dd>
          </div>
          <div>
            <dt class="text-slate-400">Geography</dt><dd>National</dd>
          </div>
          <div>
            <dt class="text-slate-400">Sectors</dt><dd>Transport, Water, Energy, Public Facilities</dd>
          </div>
        </dl>
      </div>
    </section>

    <!-- BODY -->
    <section class="border-b border-slate-900 bg-slate-950 py-16">
      <div class="mx-auto max-w-5xl px-4 grid gap-10 md:grid-cols-3">

        <!-- MAIN CONTENT -->
        <div class="md:col-span-2 space-y-8 text-sm text-slate-300">

          <!-- Challenge -->
          <div>
            <h2 class="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-100">Challenge</h2>
            <p class="mt-2">
              The government managed a fragmented infrastructure portfolio with inconsistent procurement practices,
              limited field oversight, and no unified system for reporting or documentation. Donors required a
              transparent, defensible operating model that could support multiple sectors simultaneously.
            </p>
          </div>

          <!-- Approach -->
          <div>
            <h2 class="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-100">Approach</h2>
            <p class="mt-2">
              We designed a multi‑sector PMO operating system integrating governance, procurement workflows,
              construction oversight, digital field systems, and audit‑ready documentation. The system was engineered
              to support transport, water, energy, and public facility projects under a single, coherent framework.
            </p>
          </div>

          <!-- Results -->
          <div>
            <h2 class="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-100">Results</h2>
            <ul class="mt-2 space-y-1">
              <li>• Unified PMO system covering four major infrastructure sectors</li>
              <li>• Standardized procurement and evaluation workflows across ministries</li>
              <li>• Field oversight system with digital reporting and QC/QA evidence capture</li>
              <li>• GIS‑enabled portfolio dashboard for donor and government leadership</li>
              <li>• Audit‑ready documentation trails for all procurements and contracts</li>
            </ul>
          </div>

        </div>

        <!-- SIDEBAR -->
        <aside class="space-y-4 text-xs text-slate-300">

          <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-4">
            <h3 class="text-[11px] font-semibold uppercase tracking-[0.18em] text-slate-400">
              Core Components
            </h3>
            <ul class="mt-2 space-y-1">
              <li>• Multi‑sector PMO governance charter</li>
              <li>• Procurement SOPs & evaluation templates</li>
              <li>• Oversight & QC/QA framework</li>
              <li>• Digital field reporting system</li>
              <li>• GIS portfolio dashboard</li>
              <li>• Audit‑ready documentation architecture</li>
            </ul>
          </div>

        <p class="mt-2 text-sm text-slate-300 max-w-2xl">

          planning to procurement, construction oversight, and digital system deployment.
        </p>

              01 • Working Sessions
            </p>
            <h3 class="mt-2 font-semibold text-slate-100">Targeted advisory sessions</h3>
            <p class="mt-2 text-sm text-slate-300">
              Focused, high‑impact sessions to solve specific PMO, procurement, oversight, or digital challenges.
              Ideal for rapid clarity and decision support.
            </p>
          </div>

          <!-- Model 2 -->
          <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
            <p class="text-xs uppercase tracking-[0.18em] text-slate-400 font-semibold">
              02 • Advisory Sprints
            </p>
            <h3 class="mt-2 font-semibold text-slate-100">2–6 week structured engagements</h3>
            <p class="mt-2 text-sm text-slate-300">
              Short, structured engagements that deliver frameworks, SOPs, toolkits, and decision‑ready outputs
              aligned to donor and government requirements.
            </p>
          </div>

          <!-- Model 3 -->
          <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
            <p class="text-xs uppercase tracking-[0.18em] text-slate-400 font-semibold">
              03 • Portfolio Advisory
            </p>
            <h3 class="mt-2 font-semibold text-slate-100">Quarterly or annual advisory</h3>
            <p class="mt-2 text-sm text-slate-300">
              Ongoing advisory support for PMOs, ministries, and implementing partners managing multi‑sector
              infrastructure portfolios.
            </p>
          </div>

          <!-- Model 4 -->
          <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
            <p class="text-xs uppercase tracking-[0.18em] text-slate-400 font-semibold">

    <!-- HOW WE WORK -->
    <section class="border-b border-slate-900 py-16">
      <div class="mx-auto max-w-5xl px-4">

        <h2 class="text-lg font-semibold text-slate-50">How We Work</h2>
        <p class="mt-2 text-sm text-slate-300 max-w-2xl">
          Our delivery model is built on engineering discipline, donor fluency, and field practicality.
        </p>

<script>
  document.getElementById('languageSwitcher').addEventListener('change', function () {
    const lang = this.value;

    // Trigger browser translation (Chrome, Edge, Safari, Firefox)
    if (typeof google !== "undefined" && google.translate) {
      const frame = document.querySelector('.goog-te-combo');
      if (frame) {
        frame.value = lang;
        frame.dispatchEvent(new Event('change'));
      }
    } else {
      alert("Your browser will translate this page automatically. If not, enable translation in your browser settings.");
    }
  });
</script>

      layout: google.translate.TranslateElement.InlineLayout.SIMPLE
    }, 'google_translate_element');
  }

OSHA STANDARD FOR ALL SUBCONTRACTORS and Contractor's
<!-- OSA Standard for Subcontractors -->
<section class="border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 rounded-xl p-6">
  <h3 class="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-100">OSA Standard for Subcontractors</h3>
  <p class="mt-2 text-xs text-slate-400">
    The Operational Standards Agreement (OSA) defines the minimum technical, safety, documentation, and
    performance requirements for all subcontractors operating under Global Infrastructure Advisory frameworks.
    These standards ensure consistency, transparency, and engineering-grade delivery across all sectors.
  </p>

  <ul class="mt-4 space-y-1 text-xs text-slate-400">
    <li>• Compliance with PMO governance, reporting, and documentation protocols</li>
    <li>• Mandatory QC/QA evidence submission for all works</li>
    <li>• Use of approved blueprint systems for design interpretation and field coordination</li>
    <li>• Adherence to safety, environmental, and social safeguards</li>
    <li>• Alignment with donor procurement and oversight requirements</li>
    <li>• Participation in digital field reporting and monitoring systems</li>
    <li>• Transparent change management and variation request procedures</li>
    <li>• Mandatory daily reporting for high‑risk or critical path activities</li>
  </ul>

  <p class="mt-4 text-xs text-slate-400">
    All subcontractors must sign the OSA prior to mobilization. Non‑compliance may result in corrective actions,
    suspension of works, or removal from the project.
  </p>
</section>

<!-- OSA Standard: OSHA Compliance Requirement -->
<section class="border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 rounded-xl p-6">
  <h3 class="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-100">OSA Standard: OSHA Compliance</h3>
  <p class="mt-2 text-xs text-slate-400">
    All subcontractors must comply with OSHA training requirements as part of the Operational Standards
    Agreement (OSA). In accordance with West Virginia state law (WV Code §21‑3‑22), any worker performing
    labor on a public improvement project valued at $500,000 or more must complete OSHA 10‑hour training
    prior to mobilization.
  </p>

  <ul class="mt-4 space-y-1 text-xs text-slate-400">
    <li>• Proof of OSHA 10‑hour training required for all field personnel</li>
    <li>• OSHA 30‑hour training required for supervisors, foremen, and site leads</li>
    <li>• Training certificates must be submitted before site access is granted</li>
    <li>• Non‑compliant personnel will be removed from the project immediately</li>
    <li>• Subcontractors are responsible for maintaining valid training records</li>
    <li>• Random compliance checks may be conducted at any time</li>
  </ul>

  <p class="mt-4 text-xs text-slate-400">
    These requirements ensure safe, compliant, and legally aligned operations across all infrastructure
    sectors, including transport, water, energy, mining, and public facilities.
  </p>
</section>

OSA PDF CONTENT (TEXT‑ONLY, READY FOR EXPORT)
Operational Standards Agreement (OSA)
-------------------------------------

1. OSHA & WV Code Compliance
- OSHA 10-hour training required for all field workers.
- OSHA 30-hour training required for supervisors.
- WV Code §21‑3‑22 applies to public improvement projects exceeding $500,000.
- Training certificates must be submitted prior to mobilization.

2. Safety Requirements
- Daily toolbox talks.
- Job Hazard Analysis (JHA) for all tasks.
- Incident and near-miss reporting.
- Emergency response plan compliance.

3. Documentation Requirements
- Daily reports.
- QC/QA evidence.
- Equipment certifications.
- Attendance logs.

4. Digital Systems Requirements
- Mandatory use of digital reporting tools.
- Blueprint overlays for hazard mapping.
- Real-time monitoring where applicable.

5. Technical & Performance Standards
- Compliance with PMO workflows.
- Adherence to procurement and oversight frameworks.
- Transparent change management.
- Performance monitoring and corrective actions.

6. Enforcement
- Non-compliant personnel removed from site.
- Subcontractors responsible for maintaining valid records.
- Random compliance checks may be conducted.

Downloadable Systems Map (Text‑Only)

GLOBAL INFRASTRUCTURE OPERATING SYSTEM — SYSTEMS MAP

1. PMO Governance
- Approvals, workflows, procurement pathways
- Reporting cycles and audit trails

2. Contractor Oversight
- Daily reporting, QC/QA evidence, safety logs
- Performance monitoring and compliance checks

3. Buy American Alignment
- U.S. product sourcing preferences for eligible procurements
- Integrated into procurement planning and contractor requirements

4. Safety Management System
- OSHA, WV Code §21‑3‑22, donor safeguards
- Hazard mapping and blueprint safety overlays

5. Blueprint Systems
- Structural, civil, pipeline, mining, water, energy, safety overlays
- ANSYS-style engineering environments

6. Digital Twin Architecture
- IoT sensors, GIS layers, blueprint meshes
- Real-time dashboards and alerts

7. Field Reporting

- Daily logs, evidence uploads, blueprint-linked annotations

BUY AMERICAN COMPLIANCE — MODULAR BLOCK
<!-- Buy American Compliance Block -->
<div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
  <h3 class="text-sm font-semibold text-slate-100">Buy American Compliance</h3>
  <p class="mt-2 text-xs text-slate-400">
    For U.S.-funded programs, eligible procurements must align with Buy American preferences. Contractors and
    subcontractors are required to source U.S.-made materials, equipment, and components where applicable and
    consistent with federal procurement expectations.
  </p>

  <ul class="mt-4 space-y-1 text-xs text-slate-500">
    <li>• U.S.-made materials prioritized for eligible procurements</li>
    <li>• Documentation required for origin, manufacturing, and compliance</li>
    <li>• Exceptions follow federal guidance and donor rules</li>
    <li>• Applies to contractors and all tiers of subcontractors</li>
    <li>• Integrated into procurement planning and oversight workflows</li>
  </ul>

  <p class="mt-4 text-xs text-slate-400">
    This requirement is incorporated into our PMO, procurement, and contractor oversight systems to ensure
    alignment with U.S. federal expectations.
  </p>
</div>

  <p class="mt-2 text-xs text-slate-400">
    Checklist for contractors and subcontractors to confirm alignment with U.S. sourcing expectations for
    eligible procurements under federally aligned programs.
  </p>

    <li>□ Documentation of origin and manufacturing provided</li>

    <li>□ Exceptions follow federal guidance and donor rules</li>
    <li>□ Subcontractors informed of sourcing requirements</li>
    <li>□ Procurement records maintained for audit readiness</li>

  </ul>

CONTRACTOR RISK INDEX (SCORING MODEL)
<section class="bg-slate-950 border border-slate-900 rounded-xl p-10">
  <p class="text-xs uppercase tracking-[0.22em] text-emerald-300 font-semibold">
    Contractor Risk Index
  </p>
  <h2 class="mt-3 text-2xl font-semibold text-slate-50">
    Multi-factor scoring model for contractor risk assessment.
  </h2>

  <div class="mt-10 grid gap-8 md:grid-cols-4 text-xs text-slate-400">

    <!-- Safety -->
    <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
      <h3 class="font-semibold text-slate-100">Safety (30%)</h3>
      <ul class="mt-2 space-y-1">
        <li>• OSHA compliance</li>
        <li>• WV Code §21‑3‑22 alignment</li>
        <li>• Incident rates</li>
        <li>• JHA quality</li>
      </ul>
    </div>

    <!-- Sourcing -->
    <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
      <h3 class="font-semibold text-slate-100">U.S. Sourcing (25%)</h3>
      <ul class="mt-2 space-y-1">
        <li>• Evidence completeness</li>
        <li>• Verification status</li>
        <li>• Exceptions requested</li>
        <li>• Documentation accuracy</li>
      </ul>
    </div>

    <!-- Reporting -->
    <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
      <h3 class="font-semibold text-slate-100">Reporting (25%)</h3>
      <ul class="mt-2 space-y-1">
        <li>• Daily report timeliness</li>
        <li>• QC/QA evidence quality</li>
        <li>• Blueprint-linked annotations</li>
        <li>• Data completeness</li>
      </ul>
    </div>

    <!-- Oversight -->
    <div class="rounded-xl border border-slate-800 bg-slate-900/60 p-6">
      <h3 class="font-semibold text-slate-100">Oversight (20%)</h3>
      <ul class="mt-2 space-y-1">
        <li>• Corrective actions</li>

GLOBAL INFRASTRUCTURE OPERATING SYSTEM (GIOS)
---------------------------------------------

Overview
The Global Infrastructure Operating System (GIOS) is a unified delivery framework integrating PMO governance,
contractor oversight, safety management, blueprint systems, digital twin architecture, and compliance workflows
into a single defensible operating model.

Core Components
1. PMO Governance
   - Approvals, workflows, procurement pathways
   - Reporting cycles and audit trails
   - Contractor oversight integration

2. Contractor Oversight
   - Daily reporting and QC/QA evidence
   - Safety compliance (OSHA, WV Code §21‑3‑22)
   - U.S. sourcing alignment for eligible procurements
   - Performance scorecards and risk index

3. Safety Management System
   - JHAs, toolbox talks, incident logs
   - Hazard mapping and blueprint overlays
   - Training and competency tracking

4. Blueprint Systems
   - ANSYS-style engineering environments
   - Structural, civil, pipeline, mining, water, energy, and safety overlays
   - Blueprint-linked annotations and evidence

5. Digital Twin Architecture
   - GIS layers, sensor networks, real-time monitoring
   - Blueprint mesh integration
   - Alerts, thresholds, and performance indicators

6. Compliance Ecosystem
   - Buy American alignment
   - Sourcing verification workflow
   - Procurement evidence archive
   - Compliance dashboards and command center

7. Data & API Layer
   - Compliance API
   - Authentication and access control
   - Event streaming and normalization

Purpose
GIOS provides a unified, audit-ready, engineering-grade operating system for infrastructure delivery across
transport, water, energy, mining, and public facility sectors.

DIGITAL TWIN HOSTING STRATEGY
-----------------------------

1. Hosting Model
- Cloud-native architecture (Azure, AWS, or GCP)
- No physical data center required
- Scalable compute for sensor ingestion and GIS rendering

2. Core Components
- IoT ingestion service
- GIS hosting and tile rendering
- Blueprint mesh rendering engine
- Compliance API integration
- Real-time alerting and thresholds

3. Data Storage
- Time-series database for sensor data
- Object storage for blueprint files and evidence
- Relational database for compliance and contractor data

4. Security
- Role-based access control
- Encryption at rest and in transit
- Audit logging and access trails

5. Integration Points
- Contractor Portal
- Compliance Command Center
- PMO dashboards
- Blueprint Viewer

6. Deployment Model
- Containerized microservices
- Load-balanced API layer
- Global CDN for blueprint assets

BLUEPRINT SYSTEMS — TECHNICAL SPECIFICATION
-------------------------------------------

1. Purpose
Provide engineering-grade blueprint environments for contractors, PMOs, and supervision teams across all
infrastructure sectors.

2. Supported Blueprint Types
- Structural (beams, loads, stress zones)
- Civil (roads, drainage, utilities)
- Pipeline (alignment, pressure zones, ROW geometry)
- Mining (shafts, tunnels, ventilation)
- Water (treatment, distribution, pressure maps)
- Energy (substations, transmission, renewable integration)
- Safety (hazard zones, exclusion areas, egress routes)

3. Rendering Engine
- Vector-based blueprint rendering
- Mesh overlay engine (ANSYS-style)
- Layer toggling (structural, civil, safety, GIS)
- Annotation system with geotagging

4. Data Inputs
- CAD files (DWG, DXF)
- GIS shapefiles
- Sensor data (via Digital Twin)
- Contractor field photos
- QC/QA evidence

5. Output Capabilities
- Interactive viewer
- Layered blueprint exports
- Safety overlays
- Blueprint-linked evidence trails

6. Integration
- Contractor Portal
- Compliance API
- Digital Twin Dashboard
- PMO Governance Framework

DIGITAL TWIN API SCHEMA
-----------------------

Base URL:
/api/v1/digital-twin/

Endpoints:

1. /assets
   GET  → List all assets
   POST → Register new asset
   Fields:
     - asset_id
     - asset_type
     - location (lat, lon)
     - blueprint_reference

2. /sensors
   GET  → List sensors
   POST → Register sensor
   Fields:
     - sensor_id
     - asset_id
     - sensor_type (pressure, flow, vibration, temp)
     - unit
     - threshold

3. /sensors/{id}/data
   POST → Submit sensor reading
   GET  → Retrieve time-series data
   Fields:
     - timestamp
     - value
     - status (normal, warning, critical)

4. /blueprints/{id}/mesh
   GET → Retrieve mesh overlay
   Fields:
     - mesh_id
     - layer_type (structural, civil, pipeline, mining, safety)

5. /alerts
   GET → Active alerts
   POST → Create alert
   Fields:
     - alert_id
     - asset_id
     - severity
     - description
     - triggered_by (sensor, compliance, blueprint)

6. /compliance
   GET → Compliance status for asset or contractor
   Fields:
     - sourcing_status
     - safety_status
     - documentation_status
     - risk_index

CONTRACTOR PORTAL DATABASE SCHEMA
---------------------------------

TABLE: contractors
- contractor_id (PK)
- company_name
- contact_name
- email
- phone
- status (active, suspended)

TABLE: users
- user_id (PK)
- contractor_id (FK)
- name
- email
- role (admin, supervisor, worker)
- password_hash

TABLE: safety_records
- record_id (PK)
- contractor_id (FK)
- osha_10 (boolean)
- osha_30 (boolean)
- wv_code_21_3_22 (boolean)
- incidents_reported
- last_updated

TABLE: sourcing_evidence
- evidence_id (PK)
- contractor_id (FK)
- material_name
- manufacturer
- country_of_origin
- documentation_url
- verification_status (pending, verified, rejected)

TABLE: daily_reports
- report_id (PK)
- contractor_id (FK)
- date
- activities
- qcqa_evidence_url
- blueprint_annotation_id (FK)

TABLE: blueprint_annotations
- annotation_id (PK)
- blueprint_id (FK)
- contractor_id (FK)
- description
- photo_url
- coordinates (x,y)

TABLE: compliance_scores
- score_id (PK)
- contractor_id (FK)
- safety_score
- sourcing_score
- reporting_score
- oversight_score
- risk_index
- date

BLUEPRINT RENDERING ENGINE ARCHITECTURE
---------------------------------------

1. Input Layer
   - CAD ingestion (DWG, DXF)
   - GIS shapefiles
   - Digital twin sensor overlays
   - Contractor annotations
   - Safety hazard layers

2. Processing Layer
   a. Geometry Parser
      - Converts CAD → vector primitives
      - Normalizes coordinate systems

   b. Mesh Generator
      - Creates ANSYS-style mesh overlays
      - Supports structural, civil, pipeline, mining meshes

   c. Layer Manager
      - Toggles blueprint layers (structural, civil, safety, GIS)
      - Manages opacity, visibility, and stacking order

   d. Compliance Overlay Engine
      - Safety zones
      - Exclusion areas
      - Egress routes
      - QC/QA evidence pins

3. Rendering Layer
   - WebGL or Canvas rendering
   - Vector rendering for infinite zoom
   - Real-time mesh updates from digital twin

4. Output Layer
   - Interactive viewer
   - Blueprint-linked evidence
   - Export (PNG, SVG, layered PDF)
   - Integration with Contractor Portal

5. Integration Points
   - Digital Twin API
   - Compliance API
   - Contractor Portal
   - PMO Dashboards

Global Infrastructure Operating System – full technical whitepaper (outline text)

TITLE
Global Infrastructure Operating System (GIOS)
Technical Architecture Whitepaper

1. Executive Summary
- Purpose of GIOS
- Target users: PMOs, donors, ministries, primes, contractors
- Core value: unified, audit-ready, engineering-grade delivery system

2. System Overview
- High-level architecture (PMO, Contractor Oversight, Compliance, Blueprint Systems, Digital Twin, Data/API)
- Design principles: modular, cloud-native, standards-aligned, evidence-driven

3. Core Components
3.1 PMO Governance Layer
- Approvals, workflows, procurement pathways
- Reporting cycles, audit trails, risk management

3.2 Contractor Oversight Layer
- Daily reporting, QC/QA, safety, sourcing
- Contractor Risk Index and performance scorecards

3.3 Compliance Ecosystem
- Safety (OSHA, WV Code §21-3-22)
- Buy American / U.S. sourcing alignment
- Procurement evidence archive, dashboards, command center

3.4 Blueprint Systems
- ANSYS-style environments
- Structural, civil, pipeline, mining, water, energy, safety overlays
- Blueprint-linked annotations and evidence

3.5 Digital Twin Architecture
- Sensors, GIS, mesh overlays
- Alerts, thresholds, performance indicators
- Integration with compliance and oversight

3.6 Data & API Layer
- Compliance API, Digital Twin API
- Authentication, access control, logging
- Event streaming and normalization

4. Technical Architecture
- Logical architecture diagram (GIOS stack)
- Component interactions and data flows
- Integration with external systems (donors, ministries, primes)

5. Security & Compliance
- Role-based access control
- Encryption, logging, auditability
- Alignment with donor and federal expectations

6. Deployment & Hosting
- Cloud-native deployment (no physical data center)
- Scalability, resilience, monitoring

7. Roadmap
- Phase 1: Static web + documentation
- Phase 2: Contractor Portal + Compliance API
- Phase 3: Digital Twin + Blueprint integration

8. Conclusion
- GIOS as a repeatable, exportable operating model

DIGITAL TWIN DATA GOVERNANCE FRAMEWORK

1. Purpose
- Ensure integrity, security, and responsible use of digital twin data across infrastructure programs.

2. Data Domains
- Sensor data (time-series)
- GIS and spatial data
- Blueprint meshes and overlays
- Compliance and contractor data

3. Roles & Responsibilities
- Data Owner: PMO / client
- Data Steward: GIOS operations team
- Data Producer: contractors, sensors, field teams
- Data Consumer: PMO, donors, ministries

4. Data Quality
- Validation rules for sensor data
- Completeness checks for compliance evidence
- Versioning for blueprints and overlays

5. Security & Access
- Role-based access control
- Least-privilege principles
- Encryption at rest and in transit

6. Retention & Archiving
- Retention periods by data type
- Archival strategy for audit and legal requirements

7. Compliance & Audit
- Logging of access and changes
- Periodic data quality and security reviews

8. Integration
- Alignment with Compliance API and Contractor Portal
- Data contracts between systems
CONTRACTOR PORTAL AUTHENTICATION & SECURITY MODEL

1. Objectives
- Secure access for contractors and subcontractors
- Protect compliance, sourcing, and safety data

2. Identity & Access Management
- OAuth2 / OpenID Connect
- Multi-factor authentication for admins and supervisors
- Role-based access control (PMO, contractor admin, supervisor, worker)

3. Session Management
- Secure session tokens
- Idle timeouts and forced re-authentication
- Device and IP monitoring (optional)

4. Data Security
- Encryption at rest (database, file storage)
- Encryption in transit (TLS)
- Segregation of contractor data by tenant/project

5. Logging & Monitoring
- Authentication logs
- Access logs for sensitive records (sourcing, safety, evidence)
- Alerting on suspicious activity

6. Compliance Alignment
- Support for donor and federal security expectations
- Audit-ready logs and evidence

7. Integration
- Shared identity with Compliance Command Center and Digital Twin dashboards (SSO-capable)

CONTRACTOR PORTAL AUTHENTICATION & SECURITY MODEL

1. Objectives
- Secure access for contractors and subcontractors
- Protect compliance, sourcing, and safety data

2. Identity & Access Management
- OAuth2 / OpenID Connect
- Multi-factor authentication for admins and supervisors
- Role-based access control (PMO, contractor admin, supervisor, worker)

3. Session Management
- Secure session tokens
- Idle timeouts and forced re-authentication
- Device and IP monitoring (optional)

4. Data Security
- Encryption at rest (database, file storage)
- Encryption in transit (TLS)
- Segregation of contractor data by tenant/project

5. Logging & Monitoring
- Authentication logs
- Access logs for sensitive records (sourcing, safety, evidence)
- Alerting on suspicious activity

6. Compliance Alignment
- Support for donor and federal security expectations
- Audit-ready logs and evidence

7. Integration
- Shared identity with Compliance Command Center and Digital Twin dashboards (SSO-capable)

   ↓

   ↓

   ↓

ONE‑PAGE EXECUTIVE SUMMARY VERSION

GLOBAL INFRASTRUCTURE OPERATING SYSTEM (GIOS)
Executive Summary — 1 Page

Overview
GIOS is a unified operating system for infrastructure delivery, integrating PMO governance, contractor oversight,
safety management, U.S. sourcing alignment, blueprint systems, digital twin architecture, and compliance workflows.

Problem
Infrastructure programs often suffer from fragmented reporting, inconsistent oversight, weak documentation, and
limited real-time visibility.

Solution
GIOS provides a single, defensible, engineering-grade operating model that strengthens transparency, accelerates
delivery, and ensures audit-ready documentation.

Core Components
• PMO Governance — Approvals, workflows, procurement pathways, audit trails  
• Contractor Oversight — Daily reporting, QC/QA, safety, sourcing, performance scoring  
• Compliance Ecosystem — Buy American alignment, evidence archive, dashboards  
• Blueprint Systems — ANSYS-style engineering environments with layered overlays  
• Digital Twin Architecture — Sensors, GIS, mesh overlays, alerts, performance indicators  
• Data & API Layer — Compliance API, Digital Twin API, authentication, logging  

Value Proposition
• Real-time visibility across all contractors and assets  
• Stronger compliance and sourcing verification  
• Reduced delivery risk and improved accountability  
• Audit-ready documentation for donors and ministries  
• Scalable, cloud-native architecture (no data center required)

Outcome
A repeatable, exportable operating model for national infrastructure programs.

PROPOSAL — GLOBAL INFRASTRUCTURE OPERATING SYSTEM (GIOS)

1. Introduction
GIOS is a unified operating system designed to support ministries, donor-funded programs, and prime contractors
in delivering complex infrastructure portfolios with transparency, accountability, and engineering-grade rigor.

2. Objectives
• Strengthen PMO governance and oversight
• Improve contractor performance and compliance
• Enhance safety and sourcing verification
• Provide real-time visibility through digital twin integration
• Deliver audit-ready documentation for donors and ministries

3. Scope of Work
• PMO governance framework implementation
• Contractor oversight system deployment
• Compliance ecosystem integration (safety, sourcing, QC/QA)
• Blueprint systems setup (ANSYS-style environments)
• Digital twin architecture configuration
• API and data governance setup

4. Methodology
Phase 1 — Foundation (Governance, Documentation, Blueprint Systems)  
Phase 2 — Contractor Systems (Portal, Compliance API, Evidence Archive)  
Phase 3 — Digital Twin Integration (Sensors, GIS, Dashboards)

5. Deliverables
• PMO Governance Framework  
• Contractor Oversight Operating Manual  
• Compliance Command Center  
• Blueprint Viewer & Rendering Engine  
• Digital Twin Dashboard  
• API Schemas & Data Governance Framework  

6. Benefits to the Client
• Stronger compliance and sourcing verification  
• Real-time visibility across contractors and assets  
• Reduced delivery risk  
• Scalable, cloud-native architecture  
• Alignment with donor and federal expectations  

7. Implementation Timeline
12–24 weeks depending on scope and integrations

8. Pricing Model

9. Conclusion
GIOS provides a repeatable, exportable, and defensible operating model for national infrastructure programs.

<h1>Contractor Onboarding Packet</h1>
<p><span class="label">Company:</span> Global Infrastructure Advisory (GIA)</p>
<p><span class="label">Founder:</span> Kenneth Bennett</p>

<div class="section">
  <h2>1. Project Overview</h2>
  <p>GIA is a consulting firm focused on donor-funded infrastructure, federal acquisition, and international programs, including support for the West Virginia–Ireland Education Alliance. You are being engaged to build and maintain backend systems that support payments, licensing, CRM, and reporting.</p>
</div>

<div class="section">
  <h2>2. Scope of Work</h2>
  <ul>
    <li>Implement Node.js/Express backend and PostgreSQL database.</li>
    <li>Integrate Stripe webhooks and (optionally) PayPal IPN.</li>
    <li>Build license key generation and validation system.</li>
    <li>Implement CRM endpoints for leads and purchases.</li>
    <li>Expose WV–Ireland dashboard API for internal reporting.</li>
    <li>Secure endpoints with JWT and basic rate limiting.</li>
  </ul>
</div>

<div class="section">
  <h2>3. Key Endpoints</h2>
  <ul>
    <li><code>POST /auth/login</code> – JWT authentication.</li>
    <li><code>POST /webhook/stripe</code> – payment events, license generation.</li>
    <li><code>POST /api/license/validate</code> – license validation.</li>
    <li><code>GET /api/dashboard/wv-ireland</code> – WV–Ireland metrics.</li>
    <li><code>POST /api/crm/leads</code> and <code>/api/crm/purchases</code> – CRM logging.</li>
  </ul>
</div>

<div class="section">
  <h2>4. Data & Compliance</h2>
  <p>All data must be handled securely and logged appropriately. WV–Ireland related records must be tagged with <code>program_area = "wv-ireland"</code> to support reporting and compliance. No data may be exported or reused outside this project.</p>
</div>

<div class="section">
  <h2>5. Tools & Access</h2>
  <ul>
    <li>GitHub repository (backend).</li>
    <li>Database access (PostgreSQL).</li>
    <li>Stripe test keys and webhook signing secret.</li>
    <li>Email provider credentials (test environment).</li>
  </ul>
</div>

<div class="section">
  <h2>6. Communication & Deliverables</h2>
  <ul>
    <li>Weekly status updates (short written summary).</li>
    <li>Postman collection for all endpoints.</li>
    <li><code>.env.example</code> with all required variables.</li>
    <li>README with setup and deployment instructions.</li>
  </ul>
</div>

<div class="section">
  <h2>7. Confidentiality</h2>
  <p>All work is covered by the signed NDA. All code, configurations, and documentation are the property of GIA upon payment.</p>
</div>

<div class="section">
  <h2>8. Contact</h2>
  <p><span class="label">Primary Contact:</span> Kenneth Bennett</p>
  <p><span class="label">Role:</span> Founder & CEO</p>
</div>

</body>

  .filters { margin-bottom: 20px; }
  .card { border: 1px solid #ddd; padding: 15px; border-radius: 6px; margin-bottom: 15px; }
  .tag { display: inline-block; padding: 2px 6px; background: #0a7a5a; color: #fff; border-radius: 4px; font-size: 12px; margin-right: 5px; }

<h1>Global Workforce Opportunities</h1>
<p>Jobs, contracts, training, and mentorship across all programs.</p>

<div class="filters">
  <select id="programFilter" onchange="loadOpportunities()">
    <option value="">All Programs</option>
    <option value="veterans-workforce">Veterans Workforce</option>
    <option value="wv-ireland">WV–Ireland</option>
    <option value="us-federal">US Federal</option>
    <option value="global-training">Global Training</option>
  </select>

  <select id="typeFilter" onchange="loadOpportunities()">
    <option value="">All Types</option>
    <option value="job">Job</option>
    <option value="contract">Contract</option>
    <option value="training">Training</option>
    <option value="mentorship">Mentorship</option>
  </select>
</div>

<div id="opps"></div>

<script>
const API = "https://api.globalinfrastructureadvisory.com";

async function loadOpportunities() {
  const program = document.getElementById("programFilter").value;
  const type = document.getElementById("typeFilter").value;

  const params = new URLSearchParams();
  if (program) params.append("program", program);
  if (type) params.append("type", type);

  const res = await fetch(`${API}/api/opportunities?${params.toString()}`);
  if (!res.ok) {
    document.getElementById("opps").innerHTML = "<p>Error loading opportunities.</p>";
    return;
  }
  const data = await res.json();

  document.getElementById("opps").innerHTML = data.map(o => `
    <div class="card">
      <div>
        <span class="tag">${o.program_area}</span>
        <span class="tag">${o.type}</span>
      </div>
      <h3>${o.title}</h3>
      <p><strong>Organization:</strong> ${o.organization || "N/A"}</p>
      <p><strong>Location:</strong> ${o.location || "Remote / Various"}</p>
      <p>${o.notes || ""}</p>
      ${o.link ? `<a href="${o.link}" target="_blank">View / Apply</a>` : ""}
    </div>
  `).join("");
}
